RATING: N/A
Advance through the ages of human innovation. Abstract civilization builder by drawing from the stacks of leveled discoveries to play on your growing civilization. The trick in this game is the "tuck" and "splay" of cards on how you arrange the innovation icons to manage majority to preempt, block or share other player actions. Build and transition the strength of your city as it evolves with the ages and how it interacts with other players. Brilliantly thought out powerful card interactions and unique game play with a challenging puzzle that gets crazy in the last ages.  Not for the faint of heart--very cut throat. "I demand you give me your best card (again)... Hey, where are you going? Come back."
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
Played a handful of games on a friend's pre-production copy.  I can't wait to get my own.

Just as with Glory to Rome, I liked this game from the very first play.  And also like GtR, after a few more plays I can see that there is plenty of game to explore.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
{ P - [2] 3 4 }

Wonderful head-to-head game with a great mixture between strategy and tactics. The rules are simple but mastery is elusive. There are many "goals" to pursue - score points, develop infrastructure (symbols) by melding and splaying, obtain alternate achievements, destroy your opponent's score, develop your hand by drawing cards, leap-frog to higher tech levels - and which you need to be doing right now can change at any moment. There are cards with very obvious synergy like Paper + Perspective, Fermenting + Reformation, or Philosophy + Invention, while there are more subtle combinations like Medicine + Navigation or Agriculture + Education. There are single card strategies as well such as Gunpowder, Bicycle, Democracy, and Machine Tools. Some cards are better than others, but most of the good ones are still only situationally good, and it is up to the player to recognize and foster these situations. Innovation maintains a delicate balance between consistency (a particular card you want has a 90% chance to be available, the alternate achievements are always the same) and variance (the cards are randomly ordered). There's too much chaos and not enough control for me when you add more players but with two it's something worth studying.

RATING: 3
I'm not a fan of this one due to the large amount of randomness in the game.  Many games have a random draw element, but have much less luck involved either by having fewer cad options (a large deck made up of only a few types of cards; (Tempus), A construction element before the building (Dominion), or the ability to choose instead of taking the random card (Hacienda).  In this game there is only one of each card, and the power of the cards varies quite a bit causing it to be largely luck based.

There certainly is still skill involved, but I'd rather play without that element given the choice.

RATING: 6
Disappointing, but I guess I shouldn't be surprised Innovations employed some similar mechanics from Glory to Rome.  Unintuitive card powers aside, the whole deal with tucking away score so you can earn achievements that will then make those points to actually worth something is just as burdensome as the multiple steps of putting away cards from hand to stockpile to vault or foundation in GtR.  Not to mention the fact that your tableau can change from turn to turn, having to recalculate your icons again and again becomes a process that is more work than fun.

While I don't shy away from complicated games, but I do tend to find card games that aren't streamlined to be a chore to play.  Unfortunately, Innovations just didn't click for me at all and once is enough for me to see all that it has to offer.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.25
Text-heavy, so you'll have to take your first few games slow.  Still, a game that gets requested by recently-introduced players.

Innovation is fast, fun, and changes in interesting ways from one game to the next.  Particularly, which cards are a factor can vary drastically depending on what icons you and your opponents have in play.

Overall, an intelligent game system that is somewhat marred by the fact that when you know what you need to do, you still need a little luck o' the draw to do it, but then redeemed by a short play-time and a sense of accomplishment within each game.

Don't be alarmed when early games end quickly.  More skilled play (which comes with familiarity of the cards) extends the game into its final rounds as often as not.

RATING: 6.75
Chaos.  But fun chaos.  Those who favor designing a grand engine and then having it run its course will find this game intolerable.  Once you have that engine running, someone is going to screw with it.  That's what makes the game fun, of course, but if you don't care for "take that" mechanics this is certainly not for you.

After playing a game with both the echoes and figures expansions added in, I'd say you probably don't want to play this "all in."  More like pick one expansion per game and use it.  Put the others aside.

RATING: 9
When I tried a 3-player game, I updated to a 9: This game really deserved better than '8', because the design is elegant and very nicely done, it's really an excellent game. Probably one of the most interesting "over-powered card effects" game side Cosmic Encounter. Elegant design, the messiness part of it, but it gets on my nerves a bit. Played on 3, it gets on my nerves less, as every player has 2 opponents, you are not always the main target. It does, however, require that all players are comfortable with the game to begin with. It's a LOT of concepts to get used to.
